The safe stack stores return addresses,\n15: register spills, and local variables that are always accessed in a safe way,\n16: while the unsafe stack stores everything else. This separation ensures that\n17: buffer overflows on the unsafe stack cannot be used to overwrite anything\n18: on the safe stack.\n19: \n20: SafeStack is a part of the `Code-Pointer Integrity (CPI) Project\n21: <https://dslab.epfl.ch/research/cpi/>`_.\n22: ","endLine":22,"startLine":10},{"content":"89: such as `IFCC <https://research.google.com/pubs/archive/42808.pdf>`_ with arity\n90: checks. With\n92: SafeStack alone, an attacker can overwrite a function pointer on the heap or\n93: the unsafe stack and cause a program to call arbitrary location, which in turn\n94: might enable stack pivoting and return-oriented programming.\n95: \n96: In its current implementation, SafeStack provides precise protection against\n97: stack-based buffer overflows, but protection against arbitrary It works by separating the program stack into two distinct regions:\\n14: the safe stack and the unsafe stack. The safe stack stores return addresses,\\n15: register spills, and local variables that are always accessed in a safe way,\\n16: while the unsafe stack stores everything else. This separation ensures that\\n17: buffer overflows on the unsafe stack cannot be used to overwrite anything\\n18: on the safe stack.\\n19: \\n20: SafeStack is a part of the `Code-Pointer Integrity (CPI) Project\\n21: <https://dslab.epfl.ch/research/cpi/>`_.\\n22: \",\"endLine\":22,\"startLine\":10},{\"content\":\"70: \\n71: SafeStack protects return addresses, spilled registers and local variables that\\n72: are always accessed in a safe way by separating them in a dedicated safe stack\\n73: region. It works by separating the program stack into two distinct regions:\\n14: the safe stack and the unsafe stack. The safe stack stores return addresses,\\n15: register spills, and local variables that are always accessed in a safe way,\\n16: while the unsafe stack stores everything else. This separation ensures that\\n17: buffer overflows on the unsafe stack cannot be used to overwrite anything\\n18: on the safe stack.\\n19: \\n20: SafeStack is a part of the `Code-Pointer Integrity (CPI) Project\\n21: <https://dslab.epfl.ch/research/cpi/>`_.\\n22: \",\"endLine\":22,\"startLine\":10},{\"content\":\"70: \\n71: SafeStack protects return addresses, spilled registers and local variables that\\n72: are always accessed in a safe way by separating them in a dedicated safe stack\\n73: region. The `OSDI'14 paper <https://dslab.epfl.ch/pubs/cpi.pdf>`_ mentions that\n197: on Linux the instrumentation pass finds calls to setjmp or functions that\n198: may throw an exception, and inserts required instrumentation at their call\n199: sites. Specifically, the instrumentation pass saves the shadow stack pointer\n200: on the safe stack before the call site, and restores it either after the\n201: call to setjmp or after an exception has been caught. This is implemented\n202: in the function ``SafeStack::createStackRestorePoints``.\n203: \n204: ","endLine":204,"startLine":196},{"content":"10: \n11: SafeStack is an instrumentation pass that protects programs against attacks\n12: based on stack buffer overflows, without introducing any measurable performance\n13: overhead. It works by separating the program stack into two distinct regions:\n14: the safe stack and the unsafe stack. The safe stack stores return addresses,\n15: register spills, and local variables that are always accessed in a safe way,\n16: while the unsafe stack stores everything else. This separation ensures that\n17: buffer overflows on the unsafe stack cannot be used to overwrite anything\n18: on the safe stack.\n19: \n20: SafeStack is a part of the `Code-Pointer Integrity (CPI) Project\n21: <https://dslab.epfl.ch/research/cpi/>`_.\n22: ","endLine":22,"startLine":10},{"content":"70: \n71: SafeStack protects return addresses, spilled registers and local variables that\n72: are always accessed in a safe way by separating them in a dedicated safe stack\n73: region. The safe stack is automatically protected against stack-based buffer\n74: overflows, since it is disjoint from the unsafe stack in memory, and it itself\n75: is always accessed in a safe way. In the current implementation, the safe stack\n76: is protected against arbitrary memory write vulnerabilities through\n77: randomization and information hiding: the safe stack is allocated at a random\n78: address and the instrumentation ensures that no pointers to the safe stack are\n79: ever stored outside of the safe stack itself (see limitations below).\n80: \n81: ","endLine":81,"startLine":70}],"file":"clang/docs/SafeStack.rst","repo":"github.com/llvm/llvm-project","type":"file","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/llvm/llvm-project/-/blob/clang/docs/SafeStack.rst"},{"chunks":[{"content":"279:             whence = \"before\";\n280:             cause = \"stack-buffer-overflow\";\n281:             best_beg = local_beg;\n282: ","endLine":282,"startLine":279},{"content":"271:             whence = \"after\";\n272:             cause = \"stack-buffer-overflow\";\n273:             best_beg = local_beg;\n274: ","endLine":274,"startLine":271},{"content":"142: \n143:   StackAllocationsRingBuffer *get() {\n144:     return (StackAllocationsRingBuffer *)&rb_;\n145:   }\n146: ","endLine":146,"startLine":142}],"file":"compiler-rt/lib/hwasan/hwasan_report.cpp","repo":"github.com/llvm/llvm-project","type":"file","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/llvm/llvm-project/-/blob/compiler-rt/lib/hwasan/hwasan_report.cpp"},{"chunks":[{"content":"329: \n330: uptr __hwasan_shadow_memory_dynamic_address; It works by separating the program stack into two distinct regions:\\n14: the safe stack and the unsafe stack. The safe stack stores return addresses,\\n15: register spills, and local variables that are always accessed in a safe way,\\n16: while the unsafe stack stores everything else. This separation ensures that\\n17: buffer overflows on the unsafe stack cannot be used to overwrite anything\\n18: on the safe stack.\\n19: \\n20: SafeStack is a part of the `Code-Pointer Integrity (CPI) Project\\n21: <https://dslab.epfl.ch/research/cpi/>`_.\\n22: \",\"endLine\":22,\"startLine\":10},{\"content\":\"196: The `OSDI'14 paper <https://dslab.epfl.ch/pubs/cpi.pdf>`_ mentions that\\n197: on Linux the instrumentation pass finds calls to setjmp or functions that\\n198: may throw an exception, and inserts required instrumentation at their call\\n199: sites. Specifically, the instrumentation pass saves the shadow stack pointer\\n200: on the safe stack before the call site, and restores it either after the\\n201: call to setjmp or after an exception has been caught. This is implemented\\n202: in the function ``SafeStack::createStackRestorePoints``.\\n203: \\n204: \",\"endLine\":204,\"startLine\":196},{\"content\":\"70: \\n71: SafeStack protects return addresses, spilled registers and local variables that\\n72: are always accessed in a safe way by separating them in a dedicated safe stack\\n73: region. The safe stack is automatically protected against stack-based buffer\\n74: overflows, since it is disjoint from the unsafe stack in memory, and it itself\\n75: is always accessed in a safe way. It works by separating the program stack into two distinct regions:\\n14: the safe stack and the unsafe stack. The safe stack stores return addresses,\\n15: register spills, and local variables that are always accessed in a safe way,\\n16: while the unsafe stack stores everything else. It works by separating the program stack into two distinct regions:\n14: the safe stack and the unsafe stack. The safe stack stores return addresses,\n15: register spills, and local variables that are always accessed in a safe way,\n16: while the unsafe stack stores everything else. This separation ensures that\n17: buffer overflows on the unsafe stack cannot be used to overwrite anything\n18: on the safe stack.\n19: \n20: SafeStack is a part of the `Code-Pointer Integrity (CPI) Project\n21: <https://dslab.epfl.ch/research/cpi/>`_.\n22: ","endLine":22,"startLine":10},{"content":"196: The `OSDI'14 paper <https://dslab.epfl.ch/pubs/cpi.pdf>`_ mentions that\n197: on Linux the instrumentation pass finds calls to setjmp or functions that\n198: may throw an exception, and inserts required instrumentation at their call\n199: sites. Specifically, the instrumentation pass saves the shadow stack pointer\n200: on the safe stack before the call site, and restores it either after the\n201: call to setjmp or after an exception has been caught. This is implemented\n202: in the function ``SafeStack::createStackRestorePoints``.\n203: \n204: ","endLine":204,"startLine":196},{"content":"70: \n71: SafeStack protects return addresses, spilled registers and local variables that\n72: are always accessed in a safe way by separating them in a dedicated safe stack\n73: region. The safe stack is automatically protected against stack-based buffer\n74: overflows, since it is disjoint from the unsafe stack in memory, and it itself\n75: is always accessed in a safe way. In the current implementation, the safe stack\n76: is protected against arbitrary memory write vulnerabilities through\n77: randomization and information hiding: the safe stack is allocated at a random\n78: address and the instrumentation ensures that no pointers to the safe stack are\n79: ever stored outside of the safe stack itself (see limitations below).\n80: \n81: ","endLine":81,"startLine":70}],"file":"clang/docs/SafeStack.rst","repo":"github.com/llvm/llvm-project","type":"file","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/llvm/llvm-project/-/blob/clang/docs/SafeStack.rst"},{"chunks":[{"content":"35: ; components:\\n\\n1. **StackProtector Pass (llvm/lib/CodeGen/StackProtector.cpp)**: The primary LLVM pass that inserts stack protector checks into functions. The `StackProtector` class (extends FunctionPass) and `StackProtectorPass` class (new pass manager) implement the core logic. The key function `InsertStackProtectors()` inserts prologue code to load and store the stack guard value, and epilogue code to check the value against the original. If the value differs, it calls `__stack_chk_fail()`. The `SSPLayoutAnalysis` class determines which functions require stack protection based on buffer sizes and variable properties.\\n\\n2. **StackProtector Header (llvm/include/llvm/CodeGen/StackProtector.h)**: Declares the `StackProtector` FunctionPass, `StackProtectorPass` for the new pass manager, and the `SSPLayoutInfo` and `SSPLayoutAnalysis` analysis pass that manages stack protector layout information for allocations.\\n\\n3. **SafeStack Pass (llvm/lib/CodeGen/SafeStack.cpp)**: Implements the SafeStack instrumentation pass that separates the stack into safe and unsafe regions. The `SafeStack` class handles the core instrumentation logic, and `SafeStackLegacyPass` provides the legacy pass interface. This pass protects against stack-based buffer overflows by separating return addresses, spilled registers, and safely-accessed local variables (safe stack) from everything else (unsafe stack).\\n\\n4. **SafeStack Header (llvm/include/llvm/CodeGen/SafeStack.h)**: Declares the `SafeStackPass` class for the new pass manager interface.\\n\\n5. **SafeStackLayout (llvm/lib/CodeGen/SafeStackLayout.cpp and .h)**: Implements the frame layout logic for the SafeStack pass, managing how allocations are arranged on the safe and unsafe stacks within the safestack namespace.\\n\\n6. **Stack Guard Runtime (__stack_chk_fail implementation)**: Located in libc/src/compiler/generic/__stack_chk_fail.cpp, this file implements the `__stack_chk_fail()` function that is called when a stack overflow is detected. It also declares `__stack_chk_guard` which stores the canary value. Note: While the task requested compiler-rt/lib/builtins, the implementation in this version of LLVM is in the libc library.\\n\\n7. **ShadowCallStack Implementation (llvm/lib/Target/AArch64/AArch64PrologueEpilogue.cpp and llvm/lib/Target/RISCV/RISCVFrameLowering.cpp)**: ShadowCallStack is an instrumentation mechanism implemented at the machine code level (prologue/epilogue insertion) rather than as a transform pass. The `emitShadowCallStackPrologue()` and `emitShadowCallStackEpilogue()` functions in AArch64PrologueEpilogue.cpp insert instructions to save and restore return addresses to a separate shadow call stack, protecting against return address overwrites from stack buffer overflows.\\n\\n8. **SafeStack Runtime (compiler-rt/lib/safestack/safestack.cpp)**: Provides the runtime support for the SafeStack pass, implementing the unsafe stack allocation and management through thread-local storage and memory management functions like `__safestack_init()` and `unsafe_stack_setup()`.\\n\\nThese components work together to provide multiple layers of stack protection: StackProtector adds canary-based checks, SafeStack separates stack regions to prevent unsafe accesses from affecting safe data, and ShadowCallStack protects return addresses specifically by storing them in a separate protected location.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":10811,"cache_read_input_tokens":94798,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":10811},"output_tokens":4,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"11c879ad-7b21-454b-86c4-a3681e5d9ddc","uuid":"0a2a3cf1-68ff-43de-a00d-88818235762a"}
